B0093DFMGC|4.0|As dozens of other reviewers probably mention, the premise of LOOPER is that the Master Criminal Gang of the future cannot afford to have any dead bodies around that might be used as evidence against them, so, with a Time Machine, they send trouble makers thirty years into the past (bound and hooded), to be disposed of by a team of young hitmen who work for them. The gang's inflexible rule is that hitmen in the past must kill whoever is sent back in time to them, including their older selves ... or suffer \\"grave\\" consequences.<br /><br />Joseph Gordon-Levitt plays the younger self of the film's main hitman, and Bruce Willis plays that same hitman's 30-year-older self, who at some point will be sent back for Younger-Self-Gordon-Levitt to kill.<br /><br />As virtually every viewer will expect from the beginning of this film, when Older-Self-Willis arrives in the past, he escapes from his younger self.<br /><br />SPOILER #1: However, Older-Self-Willis is not just selfishly trying to prolong his own life (while putting his younger self in jeopardy); he has a special mission in the past that involves killing the younger self of the warped-genius-villain who caused the death of a woman he loves in his future world. In other words, Older-Self-Willis hopes to change the future by changing the past.<br /><br />PLOT HOLE #1 involves the killing IN THE FUTURE of the beloved woman. Why are ANY exceptions allowed to the Rule that ALL \\"hits\\" must take place in the past? The obvious answer is: This inconsistency is needed to motivate the entire main plot about Older-Self-Willis's mission ... even if that entire plot rests on quicksand.<br /><br />PLOT HOLES #2 and #3 and #4 ... and SPOILER #2: As with thousands of other Time Travel stories/movies, this one involves a recurring LOOP. And it is clear from a couple indications that this loop has already occurred at least twice before--but this is played down, and we are given no indication whether all the past loops (which may number in the billions) have been identical (clearly the most recent ones have been), and why THIS loop might be any different from them. Further, since the warped-genius-villain has encountered an Older-Self-Willis before, why does he take any chances by sending him back to the past again (and again and again)? And, since the warped-genius-villain IRONICALLY was warped as a child BY an Older-Self-Willis's attack, HOW could-or-did he ever become warped BEFORE any Older-Self-Willis went back in time and warped him? (This seems to be a FATAL FLAW in the plot, which no viewer is ever supposed to consider, especially in terms of the ending to THIS particular loop.)<br /><br />SPOILER #3: In an earlier scene, a different hitman recognized his older self when he arrived (bound and hooded) because his older self was singing his favorite song. He released his older self and then tried to hide.<br /><br />PLOT HOLES #5 and #6: The only reason the people being sent back are NOT drugged or gagged is that we (the audience) need to be shown WHAT happens to a hitman who disobeys the gang's rule. Logic would have dictated that the gang of the future should have killed people bloodlessly, with drugs or poisons, and merely shipped the corpses to the past for disposal. Logic would further dictate that an aged hitman in the future should be sent back to a different hitman in the past, not to his younger self (and that all younger selves should be kept uninformed about the killings of their future selves).<br /><br />PLOT HOLES #7 through #57: On numerous occasions, Older-Self-Willis exhibits implausible SUPER POWERS when he is confronting multiple armed opponents. For example, while unarmed, he is able to defeat his armed younger self, having already defeated at least FOUR ARMED MEN in the future; and when he is armed, he can easily defeat dozens of armed men and cause dozens of other armed men to quiver in abject terror that he will come for them.<br /><br />BUT ... WHAT SAVES THIS FILM (for me) despite all these PLOT HOLES is the ending. My favorite kind of story, whether it is found in mainstream literature, in mystery fiction, in science fiction ... whatever ... involves the sudden disclosure of a streak of unsuspected (but plausible) NOBILITY AND MORALITY in a person who had previously seemed \\"only ordinary\\" or even \\"subhuman.\\"<br /><br />THAT is what occurs at the very end of this film ... and I will not \\"spoil\\" anyone's enjoyment of it by giving more details about it.<br /><br />If I were awarding this film a letter grade, given its roller-coaster ride of negative factors that terminate in a strongly positive and EMOTIONALLY SATISFYING conclusion, in my judgment it deserves a solid \\"B\\" ... perhaps almost a weak \\"B+\\".or me) despite all these PLOT HOLES is the ending. B00CM9JKQM|5.0|Well after living with this album for about a week now, I can safely make these statements. I think the album is the best since Mindcrime and is on par with Rage/Warning. Is that to say this album sounds anything like those albums? At moments it does. It sounds like an album that could of been between Mindcrime and Empire, taking the musical superiority of the EP through Mindcrime era and combining it with the hooky sensibilities of Empire. Is that to say it sounds dated? Oh no. This album is firmly rooted in the new century. Queensryche managed to make an album that sounds like their classic material, yet sounds fresh, new and invigorated! Songs like Redemption and Spore sound very modern peppered with some classic metal sensibilities.<br /><br />In addition this whole album calls back to their entire catalog. Appropriately enough, A World Without recalls the creepy atmosphere of Suite Sister Mary and features guest vocals from Pamela Moore! Don't Look Back and Fallout sounds like a modernized version of something you might find on their EP or Warning. Open Road even gives a vibe of something from Promised Land. I really feel there is not a bad song on it.<br /><br />The live tracks are a good bonus if you own the deluxe edition. Queen of The Reich is one of my favorite QR songs, but new singer Todd La Torre really took En Force and Prophecy and made them his own. Todd does a very good job of getting their former singer's vibe, and while occasionally sounding like him also leaves plenty of room to add his own voice. I also like how \\"new guy\\" Parker Lundgren wrote one of the best songs on the album, Where Dreams Go To Die. Somehow he was able to nail the QR sound. It is also refreshing that not only has the band accepted his input but have celebrated it.<br /><br />Now as much as i'm praising this album I am prepared to talk about some of the negative aspects. This album is master way too loud. It does sound great in my car, but on inferior sound systems it can getdistorted and crackly. Also lost is the vibe to the classic records, which of course is a problem that plagues all new albums. Does this stop me from enjoying the album? Hell no. I got over these issues very quick. I have seen some criticism of the length of the album, which I personally don't share. My attention span prefers shorter albums.<br /><br />It is fantastic to see a band that I wrote off as being dead many years ago release something that I feel i'll enjoy as much as their classic cataloge. It is also good to see that as a result, they are rebuilding their fanbase very quickly. Their former singer fired several shots across their bow, but in general, Queensryche's only reaction was to drop a monster of a release and let their work speak for itself. It is a good time to be a Queensryche fan.<br /><br />I ranked it 5 stars based on Amazon's rating, but rank it 8 out of 10 personally.

I do not say less enhancement, because Burton did add tons of clever and hilarious (albeit slightly creepy) little quips touches. I have seen it more than once by now, and still take great pleasure in the little puns and in the portrayal of characters.<br /><br />The characters in this movie are rendered with great taste.  Charlie is the unassuming and obviously pure and good-hearted boy he was in the book, as are his parents and grandparents.  Augustus, Violet, Veruca, and Mike TV are over the top, obnoxious, and despicable, in a way that makes their individual failures quite gratifying. I get a good kick out of Violet's mother, who has the most intensely expectant stare anyone has ever seen.  If any character was changed from the book, it's Willy Wonka.  I'm sure he wasn't nearly as disturbed, creepy, and awkward as he is in this movie.  The movie does, however, explain the reasons for his ways due to his tough, anti-candy father, and his isolation in the chocolate factory.  He also comes around to likeability as the movie progresses, undergoing the necessary personal growth that is required in a true hero.<br /><br />As you can see, I gave the movie 5 stars.  The entertainment value is there, without a doubt.  As is the case with many Burton films, it may be a little creepy for very young children.  But anyone with an appreciation for the quirky, the colorful, and the touching, should love Charlie and the Chocolate Factory.

B003VANOFY|4.0|**Updated 07/24/2013(see below)**<br /><br />First the good:<br /><br />The device is extremely well built, and very comfortable and this is coming from someone who has to wear glasses.<br /><br />Now, the bad:<br /><br />The software you have to install for this device is absolutely terrible.  When its running, the headset has trouble syncing with the receiver, there is frequent audio ducking (automatic volume adjustment for those that are unfamiliar with the term) even when its turned off in Windows.  Also, its seems to have trouble detecting when the mic is turned on or off.  I have to restart the software every time I turn on my machine because it incorrectly detects that the mic is activated (even though the little red light on the end of the mic says otherwise), and I have to sit there and listen to background noise if I don't.  None of these issues occur with the built-in Windows driver.  Now it makes sense why this device was built so sturdily:  because it will need to handle the inevitable abuse it will get when the customer gets frustrated with the crappy software.<br /><br />Update:<br /><br />So I've had about a month or so to get used to this device, all the while contemplating a suitable replacement.  The unfortunate news is there just isn't a whole lot of options as far as wireless gaming headsets go.  Logitech, like it or not, currently has the best offering.  Now that being said, after using the device for about a month or so, I have actually grown to like it.  That doesn't mean that the software glitches or quirks have gone away.  No, all that means is I have found ways to either ignore or workaround them and now I'm actually very happy with my purchase (hence the upgraded rating from 3 to 4).  What does that mean to the prospective buyer?  Well, I would say if you have a fairly high tolerance for dealing with buggy software then by all means, purchase this headset.  Its going to take a few weeks, but once you've gotten used to it like I have, youwill definitely not be disappointed.  If you don't have a high tolerance, you may need to look into options for wired headsets, because this is likely the best option you're likely to get as far as wireless is concerned.<br /><br />In conclusion, I will issue a cautionary recommendation for this headset, but like I stated above: buyer beware.

B004QNVQK0|5.0|In casually browsing Amazon.com's stock of Ozzy Osbourne music, I decided what other people had to say about the NEWER (2011) vinyl releases of the classic Blizzard of Ozz and Diary of a Madman albums. However, MANY of the first, easily visible reviews on the 2011 vinyl releases are for the 2002 re-issues for these albums on CD, which is COMPLETELY inaccurate as the 2011 releases feature the original recordings, intact, remastered!<br /><br />Now it is true, that prior to the 2011 releases, that the prior re-issues from 2002, were hideous abominations of what once were very great albums under Ozzy Osbourne, with the work of the late Randy Rhoads on guitar. The horror that were those releases, were that they featured re-recorded drum and bass guitar tracks, due to a lawsuit the Osbournes were going through from the session players that recorded the original tracks, over un-payed royalties. So, they eliminated their recorded tracks from the albums, and had them re-recorded by Osbourne's then current lineup in 2002.<br /><br />So without further adieu, here is what I have to say for the releases. I ended up getting the box set which included not only the vinyl records, but also the CD's and a 30th anniversary DVD, as well as a poster, coffee-table book with pictures AND a replica golden cross just like the one Ozzy Osbourne has.<br />Anyway, the vinyl records, are outstanding! Pressed on 180 gram vinyl (VERY thick vinyl versus the regular records anyone can come across when going for vinyl records), the remastering is outstanding. In comparison to the records to the CD's, it does actually sound like a different mixing was used for the records, which hasn't been heard before for these classic tracks, and a VERY much welcome new sound for the songs.<br /><br />This simply will not disappoint any Osbourne fan, and even for new listeners, I recommend the 2011 vinyl remasters for Blizzard of Ozz and Diary Of A Madman!

B00C7JGDBW|4.0|It was brave of Disney to make Oz the Great and Powerful given the fame and great respect given<br />to The Wizard of Oz (1939).  I was surprised Oz the Great and Powerful was as good as it is.<br />Much of its success is a result of some very impressive and beautiful CGI effects.<br /><br />There was a lot of disappointment, and even anger, as shown in many of the reviews here,<br />about this movie.  I don't know what people expected but I found myself fairly satisfied<br />with most of the aspects of it.<br /><br />The script is the weakest aspect, using terminology that did not exist in 1905, the time this<br />movie is set within.  People just didn't say 'WOW' and things like that, at least I don't recall<br />seeing that word in any literature from that era.  Little anachronisms like that pop up with<br />regularity and stand out like pimples on an otherwise lovely complexion.<br /><br />I didn't have a problem with any of the cast.  James Franco is very good as the charlatan<br />carnival side-show magician.  His transition to the Wizard of Oz flows naturally out of the<br />background of his character's life, and the tie-in with his Kansas life and that of his Oz life<br />is thought-provoking and touching.<br /><br />Seeing this movie made me wonder if Oz hadn't really died in the tornado and what we are<br />viewing IS his experience of heaven.<br /><br />Nods to The Wizard of Oz are frequent and apt.  The blonde woman who truly loves Oz<br />in Kansas turns out to be Auntie Em, as she tells him she has been asked by John Gale,<br />Auntie Em's husband in The Wizard of Oz, to marry him.<br /><br />Then Oz is blown away by the twister and finds Auntie Em as Glinda the Good Witch of<br />the South.  At least that is my take on it.  It's there in the script.<br /><br />The three witches are all very good as well.  Rachel Weisz is wonderful as Evanora, who<br />I think is probably the witch in the stripy stockings in The Wizard of Oz who has been<br />killed by Dorothy's falling house.<br /><br />Mila Kunis, aside from her occasional Bronx accent, is a beguiling Theodora.  Her broken-<br />heart, caused by the callous Oz, and her transformation into the<br />green-fleshed, as in poisoned by jealousy, Wicked Witch of the West, is entirely believable.<br /><br />Michelle Williams could easily have been a saccharin Disney Princess type, she looks it, but<br />she is given most of the funniest lines and she delivers them with a pretty poker face and<br />slight twitches of her mouth.  Of the three witches hers could have been the biggest flop<br />at a characterization but her Glinda is one of the big acting successes here.<br /><br />The supporting cast is by turns funny and endearing in the Disney manner.  Perhaps that<br />annoyed people, but the Quidlings, Munchkins and Dinkies are not any more cloying and<br />annoying than their 1939 counterparts.<br /><br />The China Girl, surprisingly, is not twee or irritating either, as child actors can often be,<br />especially in a Disney flick.<br /><br />Danny Elfman was the obvious choice to score this movie.  It isn't his most memorable<br />music but it is never becomes banal bombast in the action scenes, and there are plenty<br />of catchy tunes that linger in the mind but are quickly forgotten once the movie ends.<br />Unlike his best musical scores like the Batman movies, Beetlejuice, Mars Attacks! and<br />Pee Wee's Big Adventure.  I think there was a missed opportunity as Theodora and Oz<br />come over the hill and encounter the Emerald City for the first time in the movie.<br />The music does not rise to occasion in my opinion.  It is not the awesome moment<br />it could have been.<br /><br />So I give this excellent DISNEY movie four stars.  It would have been top-drawer had the<br />script been more carefully worked out.

Sadly, the horse had been neglected after their mother died. That was the first sordid, sad detail I didn't expect to read about. But it got much worse. Cheryl and her brother thought they could shoot the horse with one bullet between her eyes, and that's what they set out to do. How anyone could do this -- someone who's gone to college -- to an innocent animal for any reason is beyond me. Ignorance and lack of money are never excuses for animal cruelty. I could care less about tennis, and yet, I never once felt disinterested about the lives of everyone involved in Enfield Tennis Academy, from drills and analysis to the rampant drug and clean urine-based student economy. This is an astoundingly complex, lengthy tapestry of the interweaving lives of around 100 different characters across many years and great distance, yet even with all that the story is easy to follow thanks to the late author's brilliant storytelling style in which seemingly disconnected narratives fall into place around the two most central characters' own in just the right way to be most impactful (or at hilarious). That said, this is not a book that doesn't require a great deal of effort to read, but it is far more rewarding than difficult, where even the most mundane and uninteresting events are cast in such a light that they fascinate and draw you in, all framed by the darkly comic and 'absurdist' style D.F.W. was known for. It really does live up to the hype, even if the 'cool factor' of this book is pushed the hardest by people whose heads it sails over.

0399159347|5.0|I first discovered Liane Moriarty when my neighborhood book club chose \\"What Alice Forgot\\" one month. I found that book to be absorbing and compelling, and it made all of us ask during our discussion, \\"What would we do in the same situation as Alice?\\"<br /><br />Liane's latest book, \\"The Husband's Secret,\\" will make you ask the same question of yourself, many times over...and not just about one woman's situation, but three. When we meet our three protagonists, they're each experiencing completely unexpected life-altering events. Cecelia discovers a letter her husband John-Paul wrote to her, only to be opened after his death. While he laughs it off as a drunken, sappy letter he wrote following the birth of their first child, his suspicious behavior compels her to open it, and it opens a Pandora's box she never could have imagined. Tess gets the shocking news from her husband, Will, that he's fallen in love with another woman, but it's not just any woman, it's someone very dear to her. And Rachel, who is still devastated over her daughter's death twenty-eight years ago, learns her son and his family (including her beloved 2-year-old grandson) are about to move halfway around the world.<br /><br />That's pretty much all I can say about the plot without giving away Moriarty's delicious secrets, of which there are many. She teases the reader with hints but continually diverts our attention to keep us from guessing what's going to happen next. I became so absorbed in the stories that I read the book in two sittings in about seven hours total. Normally, I might try to guess the secrets, but with this book, I wanted to discover it as Moriarty intended for us to. I figured out the two big secrets in the pages just before they were revealed, but she still kept a few plot twists hidden for the end, which wrapped up with an epilogue that truly reminds us to not wonder \\"what if\\" and just face life as it comes. If you're the type of reader who always wants to guess the plot points in a novel, do yourself a favor and don't this time. Just go with it and focus on the characters' emotions and how they're coping with these incredible life challenges. You will get so much more out of reading this book, I promise you! The first secret isn't fully divulged until halfway into the book, which is maddening, but it does keep you turning the pages.<br /><br />Moriarty's writing feels effortless. She excels at creating compelling, relatable and sympathetic characters, even the \\"bad guys\\" (the two husbands in this story) who, like most bad guys, aren't all bad. While their wives struggle to face their new knowledge of their husbands' glaring imperfections, the reader can't help but wonder if we'd be able to see past them too. She fully lets us inside their heads and hearts, making it possible for us to feel their pain or excitement along with them. I truly found myself wondering what I'd do, how I'd feel, in the situations she created for her characters.<br /><br />This book isn't mindless chick lit by any stretch of the imagination. It will get you thinking, and feeling, in a way that chick lit can't. It's too smart for that. I wholeheartedly recommend \\"The Husband's Secret,\\" whether you're already a fan of Liane Moriarty or you just like a good foray into personal relationships, personal discovery, and the perpetual question we women all seem to ask ourselves, \\"What if...?\\"

0307719219|4.0|This book explores why some nations fail and others do not. The authors lay out their thesis early on (Pages 3-4):  \\"Countries such as Great Britain and the United States  became rich because their citizens overthrew the elites who controlled power and created a society where political rights were much more broadly distributed, where the government was accountable and responsive to citizens, and where the great mass of people could take advantage of economic opportunities.\\"<br /><br />In the process of addressing their thesis, the authors also look critically at some competing theories--geography, culture, ignorance. One comparison that serves the authors well is the fates of North Korea and South Korea, and why their well-being has diverged so widely.<br /><br />The authors provide a wide ranging analysis, including a critique of managed economies and a question about the staying power of high fliers such as China.<br /><br />One question that occurs to me, though, is how certain examples of increasing economic differences and, in the United States, Court decisions that enhance the power of economic powers might play out. Are there potential problems facing some of the democracies with increasing inequality? Only time will tell, but it is a question that arises when looking at the data.<br /><br />All in all, an interesting and important work.

0374214913|5.0|Debut novels, come in all shapes and sizes. Frankly some are fairly dire. Others start promisingly then lose their way as the author overcomplicates things or starts to waffle. A few are outstanding and Mr Penumbra's 24-Hour Bookstore certainly falls into this category. I was captivated from the first few pages, which, incidentally describe the jobless situation of Clay Jannon, the main character. This could have been quite a depressing episode, but sets the scene for the rest of the book in that the writing was excellent.<br /><br />Following this jobless period Clay manages to get employment on the night shift at Penumbra's. This is a strange, narrow, almost vertical bookshop accessed by ladders. It has a small number of more popular books up front and the strange `Waybacklist' behind. There are very few customers and they normally request volumes from the Waybacklist. Their requests are recorded in a handwritten ledger including details about the demeanour and appearance of the customer. Very strange, and, of course, Clay is eager to know what is actually going on and starts to carry out his own investigation aided by his rather geeky group of friends.<br /><br />What follows can best be described as a quest to solve a centuries old problem. Old practices and arcane ways collide with modern technology in the shape of the all-conquering Google with its huge computer based capacity to solve problems and the outcome is clever and rather unexpected. I will not give away any more of the plot as this is a book to savor and to be surprised at. What it is not, however, is a supernatural, wizardy type story which a reader of the synopsis may have assumed. It may also leave you cold if you have no feel at all for modern technology, but as you are reading an Amazon review I would assume this is not the case.<br /><br />Overall this is a wonderful book which captivated me throughout and the only disappointment at the end was that there were not another couple of hundred pages or so. I thought the epilogue, written in the future tense, was quite masterful as a finale. Highly recommended and an author to watch out for in the future.s or so. I thought the epilogue, written in the future tense, was quite masterful as a finale. Highly recommended and an author to watch out for in the future.

B00CM9JKQM|2.0|What a let down! Maybe I was expecting too much from a suppressed band, or maybe the horrible mixing and mastering as well as the short length has clouded my mind, this release is not at all up to par from what I would expect Wilton, Jackson, and Rockenfield would be a part of. The musicianship is awesome and the songwriting is strong, but overall this totally is sub par for what these guys have done in the past. James \\"Jimbo\\" Barton has really let down these guys with this recording, mixing, and especially who he allowed to do the mastering (Tom Baker). The drums are a bit too high in the mix of most tracks, the guitars are under a bit, but the worst part is the fact that everyone involved in the recording, mixing and mastering allowed Redemption, Vindication, and Don't Look Back to be very distorted and clip out in the mix. \\"Loudness War\\" compression is absurd!. Even with that peaking out in the low end, the low mid to bass frequencies are extremely low. I have to totally flip my eq to get a balanced sound from top to bottom. The Drums totally peak out everything in the opening of Redemption. I've tried it on 3 different systems and even my studio recording headphones and it's the same on all systems. Don't Look Back is the best drumming I've heard from Rockenfield in over a decade, but is marred by the production. Todd La Torre has strong chops, but his diction (pronouncing syllable correctly when singing), particularly in his consonants, is very weak, especially on the faster tempo tunes. I have a very hard time understanding what he's saying. Believe it or not, diction is important even in rock and pop music. This is also possibly a product of the bad mix. Some of the tracks have nice melodic hooks, and the final product beginning to end has an old school QR vibe of a concept album. I wasn't going to mention a comparison of Tate's Frequency Unknown project to this but after all of the negative slam on Tate's product and the praise of this album, I'll have to say FU is a far superior product. Hopefully this band will find a better producer for their next recording as that is the main fault of this 2013 self-titled Queensryche release. I realize Barton is a legendary producer, but this is plain bad. I will however look forward to buying the music in the future from both the Geoff Tate and the QR camps. I don't see Tate being able to keep the QR name after the forthcoming lawsuit. Finally, I give this 2 stars simply because there has never been a release by this band that has sounded so poor in quality, yes even Tate's FU is produced/mastered better.

B006HGXGWU|5.0|While this superb film came & went without much commercial success, I have no doubt that it'll come to be regarded as a seminal film for this era, which is so permeated with formless fear & dread. The film captures all of that fear & dread in countless aspects: apocalyptic fears, terrorism, insanity, economic collapse, disintegration of the family, drastic climate change, the end of civilization as we know it. Yes, it's about all those things ... and yet it's never ponderous, impressed with its own weight or importance. It's essentially a simple, straightforward story of one man, struggling to hold his life & soul together as nightmarish dreams & visions of doom convince him that he's slipping into the same abyss of mental illness that took his mother.<br /><br />Curtis (a magnificently understated but intense Michael Shannon) is a deeply loving husband & father, working a job that keeps him just a paycheck away from consuming debt. His wife (the glowing Jessica Chastain) sells handmade goods to supplement their income, they have a deaf daughter who needs an expensive operation. Living in tornado country, they're already under threat from the weather, as well as walking a precarious economic tightrope. Curtis is also troubled by the fact that his father ran out on his family when he was young, which makes him all the more determined & desperate to be a good father & husband. But in these times, that's harder & harder for so many working men. In fact, he's lucky to have a job at all, and he knows it.<br /><br />But then he starts having terrible dreams about a strange oily rain, mysterious storms & flocks of birds. In these dreams, loved ones become vicious killers who attack him: his family dog, his best friend, even his beloved wife. And he hears thunder while awake, thunder that nobody else seems to hear. He's approaching the same age his mother was when she developed schizophrenia, and of course he fears that he's inherited whatever genetic flaw it was that destroyed her mind. But by his very nature, desiring to be strong & self-sufficient, he's slow to tell anyone, preferring to check out books on mental illness from his woefully insufficient local library. His doctor recommends an analyst, but Curtis can't afford that; he agrees to see a local counselor, who is caring but clearly overworked & unprepared to cope with his potential problem.<br /><br />Soon he becomes obsessed with repairing & extending the old tornado storm shelter on his property, obviously the way a man who works with his hands tries to retain control of his life, by building something. Yet the dreams are getting worse, and that's starting to affect both his working & home life. Friends & family notice, become uneasy, worried -- all of which makes him even more frightened of what might be happening to him.<br /><br />Finally the crisis comes. What this is, I won't reveal ... but there's more than one crisis here, leading to an ambiguous ending that could be literal, metaphoric, or both. It'll generate a lot of discussion as to its nature. I'll only say that it had to be ambiguous, and doesn't yield to just one \\"correct\\" explanation. If it has any cinematic antecedent, it would be Peter Weir's 1977 classic \\"The Last Wave\\" -- very similar in story, but headed in a very different direction, because it deals with very different cultural material.<br /><br />Meanwhile, if you want an emotionally gripping, thought-provoking film that deals with existential dread in contemporary America, putting fantasies of zombies & sci-fi apocalypse to shame as the childish detritus they are, then this is it. There's no escapist nonsense of Stuff Blowed Up Real Good -- what blows up here is the illusion of security & normality we all need to get through everyday life in increasingly uncertain times. Most urgently recommended!oyed her mind. B008673ZAQ|3.0|I keep going back in forth about how to rate this book. Sometimes I think a 3, then a 4, then a 3.5. I guess I'll just stick with the middle and go 3.5. Here's why:<br /><br />I reread Bared to You right before I started Reflected in You because it had been 3 months since I was last engaged with these characters. Since I had everything refreshed in my mind, I thought I would dive right in and guess what happened? I was left with a regurgitation of Bared to You for several chapters. I mean seriously people, this is a contingent series. Read the first book if you want to know what happened, but don't make the rest of us suffer through endless reiterations. I had a fleeting thought to start skipping chapters, but I sucked it up and kept reading.<br /><br />The story started to move along but I found myself ridiculously frustrated. The back and forth made me want to pull my hair out. It felt like, \\"you hurt me so I hurt you and then you retaliate so I'm gonna hurt you back worse and push the limits until we are forced to have crazy sex and then repeat the cycle again.\\" I don't mind some tension and angst but DAMN. Can we get some storyline here?<br /><br />I know both Eva and Gideon have both been traumatized to the nth degree, so I can allow for some dysfunction while they try to navigate a romantic relationship in the best way that they know how. However, instead of all of the back and forth, I wish that space would have been filled with more detail and storyline. I'm all for steamy scenes, but I honestly think that the sex scenes got in the way this time. They were hot, but I was craving a progression of the storyline because I didn't want to think that I waited months to just read a book of sex scenes. It got so over the top that I started to skip through the sex in order to get to the plot. Band aid sex can only fix so much, and if it has to fix it 10 times a day, it gets really old and you end up looking like a mummy.<br /><br />This is a break down of the book:<br />15% review of what happened in the first book<br />35% sex<br />35% game playing/back and forth/break up to make up (that eventually leads to sex)<br />15% plot (and 10% occurs at the end of the book)<br /><br />One of the things that really got to me was how evasive Gideon was about EVERYTHING - his past, his past relationships, who he went to dinner with the night before, etc. There were times when he could have easily cleared things up with Eva, but he remained elusive, and for what reason? It just led to more fights and more tug of war. As controlling as he was, he thought he could keep meeting up with Corinne and Eva was supposed to be ok with that? I can kind of forgive him in the end for being so evasive because he wanted Eva's reactions to appear genuine to the police, but he could have still threw her bone. Something other than, \\"wait for me\\" or \\"just trust me\\" or \\"just feel me\\". I mean the whole point is that they are both emotionally damaged, in what world would he think that would be enough? Eva's not innocent either. I was pissed when she reconnected with a former fling, and the times she tried to make Gideon jealous infuriated me. Seriously, DO YOU WANT THIS TO END? How many times do you have to do the same thing over and over again before you realize you are just INSANE?<br /><br />There were things that I really liked. After having just reread Bared to You, I felt more involved than the first time I read about their relationship because I had time to distance it from my feelings about Fifty Shades of Grey (which I had read right before I read Bared to You the first time). I could view the story more independently instead of just looking at it as a better written copycat. Since I felt more invested in their relationship, I was able to appreciate their tender moments and closeness better while reading Reflected in You. Even though this book picks right up where the last book left off, the time I had to wait for this book to be released seemed to somehow make me feel like their relationship had been going on longer than it actually had. This was a good thing because it made their 'love at first sight' romance seem more real. I liked that we got to have more one on one time with the Eva and Gideon. I believed in their bond and I have several quotes highlighted in my kindle that I thought were touching and beautiful.<br /><br />The last 10% of the book started moving really quickly. Pieces started to fall into place and I got all excited and worked up and then, I got blue balls. Serious blue balls. I stayed up all night reading this book and by the time I finished it was light outside and I was so pissed I didn't even want to sleep. I don't appreciate being jerked around like that. I would have cut out half of the sex just to learn more about Gideon's past and be able to spend more than five minutes with the characters when they were actually getting along and not playing childish games with each other that drove me mad. Was there not enough material to make this a trilogy? Did we need to cram all of the excitement into the third book and use the 2nd book as a filler?<br /><br />More evidence that when there's a hot trilogy, wait until the whole damn set is available before embarking on the journey. When will I ever learn?<br /><br />Of course I'm going to read the last book. I need some relief. I am intrigued enough to want to know what happens with Brett, Corinne, Magdalene, Christopher Vidal Jr. and the rest of Gideon's family, Dr. Terry Lucas, and of course the much anticipated HEA of Gideon and Eva. After the emotional tornado I just experienced reading this book, there better be a HEA. As frustrated as I may seem, I did enjoy this book and if you were a fan of Bared to You, I would recommend reading it. If you are like me and hate to wait (especially when you feel somewhat unsatisfied), you may want to read this book a bit closer to when the final book of the trilogy is released.

It would not surprise me at all if some of the women that deprecate this book in their reviews do so out of denial of their own suppressed, carnal concupiscence. In fact, it would make my eyes roll!  In a still, relatively, conservative society there are those who abhor what they fear and refuse to relish in fantasy. Which, is what this entire trilogy is: fantasy!<br /><br />So, if you blatantly (or secretly) take pleasure in fantasy, read these books. They are interesting and well written for the average-slightly above average reader. I will openly admit that I did have to use the dictionary feature in the Kindle reader for some of the words, but, for me that is part of enjoying a book: taking more from it than what I had before. Books should help expand your imagination, attention and vocabulary at the very least! There are definitely parts of the book which I felt were repetitive, but, really I was too enthralled by the story to notice ... until I came across other reviewers' stinging recounts of how much they disliked this or that citing various reasons from technical things like repetition of situations, lack of variety, inconsistency of characterization, lack of realism and just plain criticism toward the books. Oh, my! (Biting my lower lip)<br /><br />Essentially, if you're an uptight control freak, you will relate to one character; on the converse, if you're a shrewd innocent who enjoys a little excitement you will definitely relate to another character. This book may help you discover hidden pining you never knew existed latent within you!<br /><br />If you are not interested in any way in erotica, this may not be the best place for you to start as there is a lot of sex. A lot. Of sex. Hot, vulgar, libidinous words for miles. So, if that makes you uncomfortable in a bad way, but you're still tingly for a little dirty reading, start with a Danielle Steel and work your way up from there, see if you really want to delve into erotica some more, maybe it's just not for you. But, if you're sated by lusty youth and a luscious storyline, jump right into the Red Room of Pain and kneel before E.L. James' intriguing characters and their torrid lovemaking in myriad situations, places and surfaces! I identify with the latter group. His characters morph to the world of the Leader, but they know when they are not happy and that drives their enlightenment. B008JFUPK8|5.0|It's hard to remake Superman these days. Batman taps into the deep psyche of vigilantism that has always haunted America, but Superman has come to embody a 1950s-style ideal of innocence  that many feel no longer applies in a cynical modern world.  Christopher Nolan and David S. Goyer came up with a simple solution. Just show Superman the way we would see him today.<br /><br />And the reality of \\"Man of Steel\\" is that Superman is terrifying.  He is all-powerful, all-knowing, and he lives among us.  He is, in essence, the ultimate terrorist.  Is it any wonder America doesn't accept him at first?<br /><br />With that perspective in mind, \\"Man of Steel\\" does what other superhero movies have failed to do (I'm looking at you, \\"Green Lantern\\"), and that's present a superhero in a realistic fashion.  Kal-El AKA Superman AKA Clark Kent (Heny Cavill) is literally Krypton's last hope, but he's also a wanderer, a cipher, and yes a hero.  Sprinkled throughout \\"Man of Steel\\" is flashbacks to the difficulty of growing up as an alien pretending to be a human, shepherded by Martha (Diane Lane) and Jonathan (Kevin Costner) Kent. Both of Superman's father figures haunt him figuratively and literally to shape who Superman was, is, and will be. It's compelling stuff.<br /><br />But this is a Superman movie, not a Batman movie, so the potential for world-shaking destruction is never far away. In fact, the level of destruction reaches uncomfortable levels -- those of us affected by 9/11 will find those wounds reopened in the face of superheroes blithely ignoring the massive casualties around them.  It's all filmed with a shaky-cam (tinged by the occasional faux lens flare), demonstrating just what Superman would look like exceeding the speed of sound.<br /><br />\\"Man of Steel\\" takes the Superman story and makes logical connections. Lois Lane (plucky Amy Adams) is the logical person to track down the alien -- not because of her sassy attitude but because she's a good reporter tracking down a lead.  Superman doesn't just decide to put on a cape -- he wears a mantle of leadership he willingly embraces. And when Superman comes face-to-face with Zod (Michael Shannon), he's staring down the regimented hierarchy of his past.<br /><br />Goyer and Nolan have pulled of a believable Superman by making him a scary possibility to face.  And yet Superman is woefully unprepared for his role as world savior -- as Zod is fond of pointing out, he's just a farm boy -- or is he? Superman's reintroduced to the DC film universe leaves Metropolis and Smallville irrevocably changed.  And if the other movies planned in the shared universe are any indication, hopefully for the better.n a lead. B00CM9JKXU|4.0|Just as the title says, this is a very good album if you aren't expecting Queensryche at their peak (Mindcrime/Empire). Let's face it, Geoff Tate and Chris DeGarmo are gone so 40% of what was the Queensryche sound has been removed. If we face the truth about any band they have 2-3 albums that are great if lucky and typically they drop off late in their careers as they mature and the popular sound of the industry changes around them (for example Metallica). The members that remain in Queensryche are not the 20-something, long haired, eye-liner wearin' rockers of the mid-late 80s/early 90s as we are not the same people that we were then. Listen to Dedicated to Chaos (an album that these guys had little to no input) and tell me that this album isn't an improvement. The last songs that even remotely reminded me of the real Queensryche were possibly Sacred Ground from Q2K or maybe Great Divide from Tribe, but most of their recent albums have been big departures from their usual sound (harmonized leads, dueling solos, melodic choruses and soaring vocals). Neither Queensryche nor any other band will ever recreate \\"the glory days\\" again, but that doesn't mean they aren't making good music because it doesn't sound like Mindcrime or Empire.<br />  Back on this album are the harmonized leads, melodic choruses and soaring vocals; the solos aren't as good, but DeGarmo is still off flying planes for a living and the reality is that he always was a better lead guitarist than Michael Wilton (no offense to Whip). Todd LaTorre is not Geoff Tate in his prime, but who is? Todd does an awesome job sounding enough like Geoff to not be a shocking departure from their sound while being himself and adding some of his own style. Scott Rockenfield pours it on when needed to drive some songs, but lays back and doesn't over-power the tune in other instances; all in all he gets to be himself again not trying to mold his playing to badly written songs. Eddie Jackson is as he always has been, theconsumate pro laying down the bass like a champ. My exposure to Parker Lundgren as a guitarist is limited at best, but he is the principle songwriter on Where Dreams Go To Die and I think that song sounds about as much as old Queensryche as any of them so I think he understand the Queensryche sound which sets them apart from other bands in their genre. Let's face it, this is a band with 3 industry veterans and 2 guys who are just getting their feet wet and they will need time to gel together and develop their chemistry as writers and performers over time. What they have accomplished on this album in the short time that they have been all been together as a complete band performing and writing music is a pretty amazing feat. In conclusion, Queensryche's best music may be behind them, but that doesn't mean they can't bring is good music now and into the future.

1932100660|5.0|Dr. Colin Campbell describes a nutritional experiment titled \\"The China Study\\" and its astounding findings. Stated simply, a Western diet rich in animal protein, is responsible for a majority of diseases of affluence like heart attack, cancer, diabetes, arthritis, multiple sclerosis etc. He thus recommends a plant based whole food to lead a healthy life. I read about several theories and dieting strategies in the past. Most famous being the low carb diet by Atkins. This book does contradict Atkins to an extent because Atkins focuses largely on carbohydrates as the villain and glorifies protein. This book does not glorify any particular nutrient. Except to state that protein should come from plants, not animals.<br /><br />The China Study was a very extensive study to determine the relationship between diseases and diet of selected counties in different parts of China. Conducted sometime in the 1970s and 1980s, and funded by US and China,  it proved that a plant based whole diet is responsible for leading a healthy life. And that animal based diet is responsible for a host of diseases. Dr. Campbell emphasizes on plant based whole food, not vegetarianism which can involve fried foods like McDonald's French Fries. There are no doubts that French Fries are bad for health. The China Study is as famous as the Framingham heart study which was conducted in 1948 and which established the concept of related risk factors such as cholesterol, blood pressure, physical activity, cigarette smoking and obesity.<br /><br />At a fundamental level, there are 3 macro nutrients-namely fats, carbohydrates and proteins. Most of our food consists largely of these 3 constituents. And trace quantities of micronutrients like vitamins. Earlier studies vilified fats. But then we found that there are good fats like unsaturated fats and bad ones like saturated and trans fats. Then carbohydrates were vilified. But then we found that there are good ones like fiber and bad ones like refined sugar. Now it is the turn of proteins. We find that there are good proteins and bad proteins.<br /><br />Dr. Campbell is very knowledgeable in the field of nutrition, he is not a medical practitioner. An accomplished researcher, not affiliated to any of the industries or business interests, he makes his case for making diet as part of medical recommendations for treating diseases. That is something which the medical community is not ready to do. Presumably because of its cozy relationship with the drug industry. Drug companies want their pills to be the sole part of any treatment. Just recommending plant based food does not make any money for the existing industry or medical practices. Cure is a more lucrative business than prevention.<br /><br />Faulty genes do have a role to play in the diseases. Dr. Campbell says that unless there is a trigger, the genes do not express themselves. No harm done without the expression. And that trigger is the animal protein. He also says that dietary supplements are not a good source of nutrients. Certainly not as good as the natural foods.<br /><br />Milk is a surprising villain in his study. And it is a staple diet for vegetarians all over. Dr. Campbell says that it contains an animal protein called Cassein. He himself being a dairy farmer, shifted to a plant based diet without any dairy products, more than a  decade ago, and leads a very active and healthy life. His family has followed suit. By the same token, mother's milk is supposed to be very healthy and safe for babies.<br /><br />Going against the grain and condemning the western diet, he ran up against stiff opposition. Entrenched business interests of dairy, poultry, pharma, and meat industry and status quo demanding medical community.<br /><br />I am impressed with his academic and research credentials and the manner in which he makes his case in a straightforward and honest manner. The book does not contain any recipes, just the nutrition concepts. The book was clearly an eyeopener ! It is certainly one of the best nutrition books I ever read.

B00CRJSWBQ|5.0|I decided to catch up with the latest tech and upgrade from an 8 year old dell model which frankly got so useless over time that I've hardly used it in the last 5 years. Beginning as a noob to all things pc related I did my research and watched some YouTube vids on building a dedicated high end pc (newegg has an excellent three part tutorial for any you noobs wanting to test the water). Asus was a brand recommended to me by a friend for their quality mobos. Having heard about the imminent release of Intel's new Haswell processors I decided to wait a couple more weeks before taking the plunge all the while doing more research by the end of which I was all raring to go and picked up this little bad boy on release day. I'm glad I waited, moving on...<br /><br />Features and connectivity - where do I begin, there's just so much of it. The good thing is it doesn't feel cramped inside a Fractal Design R4 case and all the ports are located in convenient places so as to keep cable management neat and tidy. This of course helps with airflow within the case and is visually appealing for any aspiring tech geek. There are plenty of 'pro' reviews out there on this so I won't bore you with what's already been covered like specs and functionality, the information is all readily available. I will however briefly cover some of its attributes that really surprised me and made me feel it was money well spent.<br /><br />Overclocking - Asus makes it easy. Ok it probably won't suit some of you veterans of the pc world who will prefer to go beyond and manually over clock (which of course is covered by this board in its UEFI Bios) but for us beginners it was as simple as flicking a switch. The TPU switch on the mobo has three settings, off, 1 and 2. At the default setting (off) it runs the processor at its stock speed (3.5ghz Intel I7). I switched it to 1, turned the pc on and by god, the speed jumped up to around 4ghz. Then using the excellent user friendly Asus AI suite software (more on this later) I was able to up the performance to 4.4ghz simply by pressing a few buttons using its 4-way optimisation feature, it's all automated and more importantly safe so I know I can't damage anything.<br /><br />Asus AI Suite software - Asus makes it easy. This software is multifaceted and you could use it to not only further tweak your overclocking settings but a host of other clever things like monitor system performance and stability, temperature, fan control and a lot more I have yet to discover or use. You could even set it so it charges your usb powered mobile device whilst the pc is off, not only does it work with my iPhone but also the power hungry iPad. Superb I thought as it saves me buying yet another overpriced charger from Apple.<br /><br />Asus UEFI Bios - Asus makes it easy. I must admit a lot of this stuff is cryptic to me (must be heaven for all you tweakers) so I won't go into it too much but I was easily able to navigate myself around to set XMP feature for overclocking RAM to the manufacturer recommended speed. Again this was done simply by pressing a couple of buttons on the keyboard and the mobo took care of all the rest. I know I could get more out of my sexy looking Corsair RAM (did I just say that?) by manually overclocking but I'll save that for a time when I know what I'm doing. In the meantime 1866mhz is plenty I should think. The user interface looks and operates more like a Windows programme than what I would normally associate with a BIOS. Very neat.<br /><br />Wifi & Bluetooth - The wifi reception is perfect, I am comfortably reaching 60mb download and 20mb upload speeds, near the limits of my broadband package and in a room that usually has average reception from the router. The wifi adaptor is really quite slick with a built in magnet so it sticks firm on the metal case and I can quite easily move it around. There seems to be an issue however when using Bluetooth (e.g. Playing back music from my phone) which my techy friend tells me is due to interference caused by the strong wifi signal. I have no idea how or if this can be resolved but since I hardly ever use Bluetooth with my pc it certainly isn't in my list of priorities.<br /><br />Audio quality - This is an area that I'm actually quite comfortable with for a change here. If you had asked me if pc audio can be taken seriously about a couple months ago I would have stuck my nose up and said categorically 'no'. Having heard it on many occasions on different PCs and on different audio systems it was, as far as I was concerned, a noisy and dirty place: switching power supplies, poor noise floor and a bunch of other audio gremlins that leapt out of the built in sound card and associated circuitry to cause a disastrous audio experience. The usual mantra amongst the audiophile community to bypass this issue is to recommend an external DAC at the least connected via USB (ideally Asynchronous). Well it looks like I'll have to eat my own hat, the sound from the built in sound card is refreshingly pure with no obvious audible artefacts, I even brought up my stereo DAC from the main system downstairs just to do a comparison and hooked it up via Asynchronous USB using J River media centre and bit-perfect output. Now at this point some audiophile may suggest well it might be the limitation of your pc speakers (corsair SP2500) being able to resolve any difference. Maybe. But I also hooked it up to my Sennheiser HD650 headphones and could hardly tell any difference, granted the stereo DAC rolled off the treble a bit and there was a tiny bit more oomph in the bass but that's because it was tuned and setup to sound like that. So sound quality wise, I can't complain, this mobo has far exceeded my expectations. In fact it has done more than that, it has changed in me a long held view about audio output from PCs in general. It seems the PC world certainly has progressed in leaps and bounds over the years.<br /><br />So in conclusion, the Deluxe motherboard is just vast in terms of features and connectivity, the components and general standard of build is of a high standard. To support the hardware it has excellent user friendly BIOS and software which it seems Asus has spent many man hours in designing and tweaking. I know its only a matter of opinion but I think it looks very nice with the gold coloured highlights on a black background. It has a lot of neat features and the flexibility to keep me going for a long time, all for just Â£220 which I think really is a bargain.

Now in its second edition, it has become highly regarded as an authoritative work of reference in one convenient volume and therefore ideal, either for those appearing before the tribunal and their advisors, or for members of the tribunal themselves.<br /><br />The purpose of a mental health tribunal is fundamentally to determine whether an individual should, or should not, be detained under the Mental Health Act (MHA 1983). As author Jonathan Butler points out, the tribunal was `in part a product of the ECHR, frequently referred to as the European Convention on Human Rights.  While such tribunals had mainly advisory powers, the MHA 1983 gave rise to a tribunal `able to deal with the needs of a patient in a more extensive manner'.<br /><br />In the words of the author's colleague, Kris Gledhill, quoted in the preface, `the law relating to detention on the basis of mental disorder and the tribunal at the centre of applications for release should be settled and certain, given that it involves deprivation of liberty and a vulnerable population, two factors that make it important that it be clear.'  Clarity and usefulness to all who participate in a tribunal is therefore the main aim of this book.<br /><br />The book features detailed commentary and explanation of the organization, procedure and jurisdiction of the tribunal in Parts A and B, with the focus on both non-offender patients in Part C and offender patients in Part D.  Part E,  `Supporting Materials' includes codes of practice,  MHRT rules and a glossary of medical terms, plus Civil Procedure Rules 1998, Claims for Judicial Review - and much more.<br /><br />This being the latest edition, there is much new material which takes into account new procedural developments in the tribunal system, together with the continuing development of the Mental Health Act 1983, the Mental Capacity Act 2005 -- and all important case law that has emerged since the publication of the previous edition.<br /><br />Anyone doing further research in this difficult area will value the almost forty pages containing tables of cases, statutes, statutory instruments and EC and International material.  There is also a glossary of medical terms, including common medications... a further list of common medications... and list of abbreviations.<br /><br />Given the resources that this book provides, specialist legal practitioners, as well as psychiatrists, psychologists and social workers should regard it as an essential acquisition. 1908407336|5.0|OF EXTRADITION LAW FOR THE PRACTITIONER<br /><br />An appreciation by Phillip Taylor MBE and Elizabeth Taylor of Richmond Green Chambers<br /><br />Extradition law is often misunderstood by the practitioner who may have a rather sketchy overview of the subject and the new processes.  To the rescue comes \\"Extradition Law\\" by solicitors Edward Grange and Rebecca Niblock which sets out how the procedures operate with great clarity.<br /><br />The Legal Action Group has excelled itself with this new title because it covers one specialist area of law which is gaining much greater prominence today, namely the European Arrest Warrant (EAW).<br /><br />The book begins with a useful series of commentaries in 12 detailed chapters.  The remainder of the book has 7 highly practical appendices covering the following areas: framework decision on the EAW; relevant sections of the Extradition Act; EAW validity checklist; EAW first appearance checklist; bail checklist; case management form; and the application notice on Form N161.<br /><br />As Senior District Judge Howard Riddle writes in the Foreword, \\"a person arrested on an extradition warrant needs help\\". He goes on to say that \\"extradition is stressful, usually more stressful than domestic criminal proceedings\\". The importance of the first hearing is stressed with the point that the lawyer must `'get it right'.<br /><br />With the rise in the number of hearings - 100 new cases a year at the old Bow Street court before the new legislation to 1,700 a year at Westminster Magistrates' Court - and Divisional Court/Supreme Court decisions it is clear that `the potential for litigating a new point is far from exhausted' as Riddle.  To add to this, there are now 4 extradition courts working every day, plus the court on a Saturday to handle the increased workload.<br /><br />Extradition law is an area where both Defendants and the Judiciary rely greatly on the expertise of the specialist lawyer.  Grange and Niblock have filled the gap in the already available texts on extradition with this work and, as Riddle says, it not only will be but is `a very significant addition to the literature in this field'.<br /><br />The last word goes to the authors who say in the Preface that the book is written with the duty solicitor in mind and no one can disagree that `the book is one that will fit handsomely into the busy lawyer's bag and prove invaluable as a tool to tackle the minefield of extradition law and procedure'. 1846615518|5.0|[[VIDEOID:mo1SF0DAR10AISK]]A STEP BY STEP MANUAL OF THE COMPLETE DUE DILIGENCE PROCESS<br /><br />An appreciation by Phillip Taylor MBE and Elizabeth Taylor of Richmond Green Chambers<br /><br />Much have we heard of due diligence of late. As expert author Vanessa Williams explains, the difficult economic conditions of recent years `have lifted due diligence to higher prominence'.  One might add that in the wake of stringent and very recent anti-bribery legislation, awareness of the dire necessity for due diligence is now very prominent indeed.<br /><br />In this clear and concise work of reference, the author describes due diligence as `the process of investigation through which a potential purchaser gains a complete understanding of the target business or its assets for acquisition, evaluating both the strengths and the weaknesses of the business and reaching conclusions as to whether to proceed with a purchase, reduce the price or restructure the transaction.'<br /><br />Based on the time-honoured principle of `caveat emptor' due diligence is a process by which, for example, solicitors and other parties working on mergers and acquisitions, management buy-outs, or buy-ins, or other corporate financial transactions, check out the company they may seek to acquire -- and a very thorough and systematic check it is.<br /><br />Writing in the preface, Williams notes that, interestingly, there is often a slight disconnect between the need for a rigorous, thoroughly professional and essentially watertight due diligence process and what she has observed as the relative inexperience of the practitioners who typically carry it out, many of whom are at the beginning of their careers.  But what they may lack in in-depth understanding of due diligence, however, might be made up for by their acquiring a copy of this book.<br /><br />The book's sub-title is indicative.  It is indeed a step-by-step manual of the complete due diligence process from start to finish.  Here in a single handbook is everything that the company and its professional advisers need regarding the transaction itself, as well as points of concern, precedents and potential pitfalls.<br /><br />Approximately one quarter of the guide takes the reader through the procedure itself, including reviewing all relevant information, from accounts... to general and intangible assets to... yes, anti-bribery and corruption and other issues including real property and software.  Further specific issues, including post-completion issues, are examined in depth.<br /><br />The remaining three-quarters of the book then goes on to list sample documents and explanatory notes supplemented by general and specific comments. This new edition, therefore, contains much new material. 0807014273|5.0|This is a hard review to write. What do you say about one of the greatest books you've ever read?<br /><br />I'll begin like this: Have you ever seen two people engaged in one-upmanship? Who has it worst? The one guy or the other girl? It's a competition with little merit and little is gained by the spectators. One or the other is crowned the King or Queen of Misery. Whoopie-doo.<br /><br />It's a truism everyone goes through hard times. Few have gone through a hard time that tests the mettle of ones heart, mind and health more than a Nazi concentration camp. That's not the point, though. Neither is it just how much time Frankl spent in Auschwitz versus some other less-infamous camp. What matters is what the experience did to Frankl and what he teaches us of those experiences. After reading this book I feel ever so slightly wiser because I have tried to vicariously understand the horror of the concentration camp. As well written as this book is, language is an imperfect medium. On some level, I will never understand the horror. I never lived it. Nor do I ever want to.<br /><br />I gained a lot from this book in some non-concrete ways. Frankl would have been an amazing person to have met or to have heard speak. Even if you read \\"Search for Meaning\\" merely to find out what the camps were like, it succeeds. If you're such a person, you might want to skip the last half where he discusses his theory. I've seen documentaries on the holocaust and been to the museum in Washington, D.C. To me, all of those experiences pale to reading this book. Frankl discusses aspects to camp life that are relatively untouched in those popularized exhibitions. For example, the mindset of the inmates or the Capos. Those kinds of memories would be uncomfortable for most. Heck, thinking about genocide is uncomfortable for most. Frankl is an unflinching witness.<br /><br />For those who are brave enough to read this book, it's well worth it.

Jeeves' vastly superior intellect is regularly pressed into service to help his employer, young, rich, idle Bertie Wooster, to get \\"out of the boullion,\\" where he has a habit of landing.<br /><br />Bertie Wooster has just enough bean power to recognize Jeeves' value, and expresses it this way: \\"The man's a genius. From the collar upward he stands alone.\\" Jeeves consistently disapproves of Bertie's sartorial decisions, and its always funny to watch Bertie try to withstand the stress. When Bertie defiantly grows a moustache, \\"it cut Jeeves to the quick. He couldn't stick the thing at any price, and I had been living ever since in an atmosphere of bally disapproval till I was getting jolly well fed up with it. What I mean is, while there's no doubt that in certain matters of dress Jeeve's judgment is absolutely sound and should be followed, it seemed to me it was getting a bit too thick if he was going to edit my face as well as my costume.\\"<br /><br />The series of stories have a similar theme: one of Bertie's friends, like him part of idle and intellectually challenged rich, get into some spot of trouble, from which Jeeves helps rescue them. But the language is so inventive and so consistently funny, and the predicaments are also very amusing, that the other \\"sameness\\" doesn't detract one bit.

I was excited about Twyla from the stock picture but when she arrived I was even more impressed with how adorable she is. Twyla is a smaller sized doll (the same size as Howleen). The thing I like the most is the spider and web theme she has throughout her outfit and accessories (I didn't even notice it on the stock pictures). Twyla's hair is mostly seafoam green with stripes of cobalt blue and a very few thin dark purple stripes. It is slightly wavy with blunt cut bangs. Her skintone is a beautiful shade of lavender except for her hands which are metallic grey that fades out as it goes up her forearm towards her elbow. She also has wispy metallic grey designs on her lower legs. Her eyes are really lovely being mostly pink and purple and having larger black pupils (I imaging these enlarged pupils come from her need to see in the dark. That is a very clever attention to detail on the part of the designer). Her makeup is minimal but it works for her. Her upper eye has black eyeliner and eyelashes with her lower eyeliner and eyelashes being purple. She has a line of lavender painted under her lower eye but it is so close to her skin color you can hardly detect it. Her lips are a stunning shade of metallic mauve. Her eyebrows are green which stands out nicely against the color of her skin. Her 3/4 sleeve top is a dark purple with black stripes down printed on it with little spiders dotted along the stripes. The shirt has a black collar with a bow tied at the front. Her three tiered skirt is a mix of a black background with a seafoam green swirl design with a purple tulle ruffle sewn at the end of each tier. Her belt is seafoam green plastic with a skullette right at the center, and dangling down from the skullette is a small spider. Her earrings are light metallic silver escutcheons with little doorknobs and even a keyhole. On her left wrist she wears two thin lavender and one thin black bracelet. On her right wrist she wears a seafoam green bracelet that has a spider web that is shaped like skullette with three tiny spiders hanging from that. Her adorable dark purple kisslock purse features a black strap, intricate molded scrollwork and a light green skullette shaped web with five minatures spiders dangling from the web painted on the front. Her shoes are dark purple oxford style pumps with green laces with spiders at the ends and and a black scrolled heel and platform. Her pet dust bunny Dustin is also very cute. He is lavender with a little pink nose, a grey button for a right eye, and a green stitch for a left eye. His little ears are standing up and he has the cutest surprised expression. He is quite large, (in fact I think other than Nightmare he is probably the largest MH pet so far). Twyla comes with a black stand and brush and her diary. Overall I think Twyla is a fantastic addition to any monster high collection.
